<p><b>Timo Werner</b> (<small>German pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[timo vn]</a></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> born 6 March 1996) is a German professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Striker_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Striker (association football)">striker</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany national team</a>. 
</p><p>Werner began his senior club career in 2013 playing for <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a>, becoming the club's youngest debutant and youngest ever goalscorer. He signed with <a href="/wiki/RB_Leipzig" title="RB Leipzig">RB Leipzig</a> in 2016, aged 20, in a then club record <a href="/wiki/Transfer_(association_football)" title="Transfer (association football)">transfer</a> worth 10&#160;million, where he set the record as the youngest player to reach 150 and 200 appearances in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>. Werner also finished as the league's second highest goalscorer in the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Bundesliga" title="201920 Bundesliga">201920 season</a>. 
</p><p>A German international, Werner was a prolific goalscorer at youth international level for Germany, scoring 34 goals in 48 appearances across the various age group levels. Werner made his senior debut in 2017 and helped Germany win the <a href="/wiki/2017_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2017 FIFA Confederations Cup">2017 FIFA Confederations Cup</a>, winning the Golden Boot as the tournament's highest goalscorer. He also represented Germany at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timo_Werner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Werner was born in <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>, Baden-Württemberg<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> to Günther Schuh, a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a>, and Sabine Werner.<sup id="cite_ref-Rise_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rise-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timo_Werner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="VfB_Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timo_Werner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: VfB Stuttgart">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Timo_werner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Timo_werner.jpg/170px-Timo_werner.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Timo_werner.jpg/255px-Timo_werner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Timo_werner.jpg/340px-Timo_werner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="691" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Timo_werner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Werner with <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a> in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Werner played for TSV Steinhaldenfeld before joining <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a>'s academy in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> During the 201213 season, he was promoted to the U-19 team despite only being 16-years old at the time. He scored 24 goals that season and was rewarded for his form when he won the Gold U-17 <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Walter_Medal" title="Fritz Walter Medal">Fritz Walter Medal</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Rise_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rise-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Werner made his senior debut later that year in a <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round" title="201314 UEFA Europa League qualifying phase and play-off round">201314 UEFA Europa League qualifying phase</a> match against <a href="/wiki/PFC_Botev_Plovdiv" class="mw-redirect" title="PFC Botev Plovdiv">PFC Botev Plovdiv</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rise_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rise-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Upon doing so, he became the youngest player to ever play in an official match for Stuttgart at the age of 17 years, four months and 25 days, breaking the record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Poschner" title="Gerhard Poschner">Gerhard Poschner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rise_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rise-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BLF_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BLF-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In the following weeks he also became Stuttgart's youngest ever player in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>, and youngest ever goalscorer after netting his first goal for the club against <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BLF_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BLF-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He broke another record on 10 November when he scored a <a href="/wiki/Brace_(sports)#In_sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Brace (sports)">brace</a> in a 31 win over <a href="/wiki/SC_Freiburg" title="SC Freiburg">SC Freiburg</a>, thereby becoming the youngest player in Bundesliga history to score two goals in one game.<sup id="cite_ref-YG_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YG-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On his 18th birthday Werner signed a professional contract until June 2018 with VfB Stuttgart. He went on to score 13 goals in 95 league appearances, during which time he became the youngest player to make 50 Bundesliga appearances in the competition's history.<sup id="cite_ref-Rise_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rise-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ten_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ten-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The record was later broken by <a href="/wiki/Kai_Havertz" title="Kai Havertz">Kai Havertz</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Stuttgart were relegated in May 2016 which prompted him to join newly promoted club <a href="/wiki/RB_Leipzig" title="RB Leipzig">RB Leipzig</a> the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RBL_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RBL-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RB_Leipzig">RB Leipzig</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timo_Werner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: RB Leipzig">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20191002_Fu%C3%9Fball,_M%C3%A4nner,_UEFA_Champions_League,_RB_Leipzig_-_Olympique_Lyonnais_by_Stepro_StP_0078_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/20191002_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_UEFA_Champions_League%2C_RB_Leipzig_-_Olympique_Lyonnais_by_Stepro_StP_0078_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-20191002_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_UEFA_Champions_League%2C_RB_Leipzig_-_Olympique_Lyonnais_by_Stepro_StP_0078_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/20191002_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_UEFA_Champions_League%2C_RB_Leipzig_-_Olympique_Lyonnais_by_Stepro_StP_0078_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-20191002_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_UEFA_Champions_League%2C_RB_Leipzig_-_Olympique_Lyonnais_by_Stepro_StP_0078_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/20191002_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_UEFA_Champions_League%2C_RB_Leipzig_-_Olympique_Lyonnais_by_Stepro_StP_0078_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-20191002_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_UEFA_Champions_League%2C_RB_Leipzig_-_Olympique_Lyonnais_by_Stepro_StP_0078_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="953" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20191002_Fu%C3%9Fball,_M%C3%A4nner,_UEFA_Champions_League,_RB_Leipzig_-_Olympique_Lyonnais_by_Stepro_StP_0078_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Werner playing for <a href="/wiki/RB_Leipzig" title="RB Leipzig">RB Leipzig</a> in 2019</div></div></div>
<p>On 11 June 2016, Werner agreed to a four-year contract with RB Leipzig for a reported transfer fee of 10&#160;million, the largest in the club's history.<sup id="cite_ref-RBL_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RBL-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On 26 September 2016, he became the youngest player to play in 100 Bundesliga matches when he appeared in a fixture against <a href="/wiki/1._FC_K%C3%B6ln" title="1. FC Köln">1. FC Köln</a> at the age of 20 years and 203 days.<sup id="cite_ref-YP_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YP-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In doing so, he bettered the record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Julian_Draxler" title="Julian Draxler">Julian Draxler</a> by 22 days, although he was again surpassed by Havertz in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Werner ended the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Bundesliga" title="201617 Bundesliga">201617 Bundesliga</a> season with 21 goals, making him the leading German goalscorer in the division, and helped RB Leipzig qualify for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> for the first time in the club's history.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2018, in a match against his former club, Stuttgart, Werner became the youngest player to reach the milestone of 150 Bundesliga appearances, eclipsing the record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Charly_K%C3%B6rbel" title="Charly Körbel">Charly Körbel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-one50_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-one50-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Later that month he helped Leipzig defeat <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> for the first time ever when he scored the winning goal in a 21 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He ultimately went on to score 13 goals and record seven assists for the season.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 October 2018, Werner scored two goals in a 60 league win over <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a>, the first of which was his 50th Bundesliga goal. The result was also RB Leipzig's biggest ever win in the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The following month, he scored a twice in a 30 league win over <a href="/wiki/Hertha_BSC" title="Hertha BSC">Hertha BSC</a> and in doing so recorded the tenth competitive brace of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He reached the milestone of 10 league goals for the season on 16 December after scoring twice in a 41 win over <a href="/wiki/1._FSV_Mainz_05" title="1. FSV Mainz 05">Mainz 05</a>. His double against Mainz was his fifth brace of the campaign, meaning that by that stage of season every time he scored in a match he went on to score a brace.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> On 27 January 2019, he made his 100th appearance for RB Leipzig when he started in a 40 league win over <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Fortuna Düsseldorf">Fortuna Düsseldorf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He became the first player to score 50 Bundesliga goals for the club on 4 May when he scored once and assisted another in a 33 draw with Mainz.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Werner scored his first Bundesliga hat-trick in a 31 away victory against <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a> on 30 August 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He made his 100th league appearance for the club on 5 October, during a 11 draw with <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> At the start of the following month, he scored another hat-trick and recorded three assists to guide Leipzig to an 80 win over Mainz, their biggest-ever win in the Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On 23 November, he became the youngest ever player to reach the milestone of 200 Bundesliga appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-2h_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2h-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his final match as a Leipzig player on 27 June 2020, Werner scored both of his side's goals in a 21 win away to <a href="/wiki/FC_Augsburg" title="FC Augsburg">Augsburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LeipzigRecord_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeipzigRecord-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Hence, he finished his tenure at Leipzig with 95 goals, to become the club's record goalscorer, overtaking <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Frahn" title="Daniel Frahn">Daniel Frahn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LeipzigRecord_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeipzigRecord-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chelsea">Chelsea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timo_Werner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Chelsea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 18 June 2020, Werner agreed to sign for English <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, who activated his £47.5&#160;million release clause, on a five-year contract. He joined the club on 1 July.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
He made his league debut with the club on 14 September, in a 31 away win against <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton &amp; Hove Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On 29 September, Werner scored his first goal for Chelsea in a 11 draw against <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> which they lost 54 on penalties in the fourth round of the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_EFL_Cup" title="202021 EFL Cup">EFL Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On 17 October, Werner scored his first Premier League goals with a brace and assisted Kai Havertz for the third as Chelsea drew <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> 33 at home.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 28 October, he scored his first Champions League goal for Chelsea, a penalty against Russian side <a href="/wiki/FC_Krasnodar" title="FC Krasnodar">Krasnodar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On 15 February 2021, Werner scored in a 20 win over <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> in the Premier League and ended his 14-game goal drought in the league.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timo_Werner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2019-06-11_Fu%C3%9Fball,_M%C3%A4nner,_L%C3%A4nderspiel,_Deutschland-Estland_StP_2057_LR10_by_Stepro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/2019-06-11_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_L%C3%A4nderspiel%2C_Deutschland-Estland_StP_2057_LR10_by_Stepro.jpg/170px-2019-06-11_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_L%C3%A4nderspiel%2C_Deutschland-Estland_StP_2057_LR10_by_Stepro.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/2019-06-11_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_L%C3%A4nderspiel%2C_Deutschland-Estland_StP_2057_LR10_by_Stepro.jpg/255px-2019-06-11_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_L%C3%A4nderspiel%2C_Deutschland-Estland_StP_2057_LR10_by_Stepro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/2019-06-11_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_L%C3%A4nderspiel%2C_Deutschland-Estland_StP_2057_LR10_by_Stepro.jpg/340px-2019-06-11_Fu%C3%9Fball%2C_M%C3%A4nner%2C_L%C3%A4nderspiel%2C_Deutschland-Estland_StP_2057_LR10_by_Stepro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3162" data-file-height="3162" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2019-06-11_Fu%C3%9Fball,_M%C3%A4nner,_L%C3%A4nderspiel,_Deutschland-Estland_StP_2057_LR10_by_Stepro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Werner with <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> in 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Werner represented Germany at <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_youth_football_team" title="Germany national youth football team">youth level</a>, playing for the U15, U16, U17, U19 and <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_under-21_football_team" title="Germany national under-21 football team">U21</a> teams, scoring 34 goals in 48 matches overall. In 2010, he scored a hat-trick on his first appearance for Germany U15 in a match against Poland. Two years later, he was a part of the Germany team that finished runner-up in the <a href="/wiki/2012_UEFA_European_Under-17_Championship" title="2012 UEFA European Under-17 Championship">2012 UEFA European Under-17 Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ten_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ten-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Werner was called up to the <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">German senior squad</a> in 2017 by head coach <a href="/wiki/Joachim_L%C3%B6w" title="Joachim Löw">Joachim Löw</a> for the friendly against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> and the 2018 World Cup qualification match against <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_national_football_team" title="Azerbaijan national football team">Azerbaijan</a> on 22 and 26 March 2017 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 May 2017, Werner was named in Germany's squad for the <a href="/wiki/2017_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2017 FIFA Confederations Cup">2017 FIFA Confederations Cup</a> held in Russia. He appeared as a substitute for <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Wagner" title="Sandro Wagner">Sandro Wagner</a> in the team's opening game of the tournament against <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> before scoring his first two international goals when selected to start in Germany's final group match against <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> on 25 June.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, Werner scored Germany's third goal in a 41 semi-final victory over <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 2 July 2017, Werner assisted <a href="/wiki/Lars_Stindl" title="Lars Stindl">Lars Stindl</a>'s tournament winning goal in the <a href="/wiki/2017_FIFA_Confederations_Cup_Final" title="2017 FIFA Confederations Cup Final">2017 FIFA Confederations Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_football_team" title="Chile national football team">Chile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> With three goals and two assists, Werner was awarded the tournament's Golden Boot.<sup id="cite_ref-CFC_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CFC-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 June 2018, Werner was included in Germany's final 23-man squad for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> He made his first <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> appearance on 17 June, starting in a 10 loss to Mexico in Germany's opening match.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> He featured in both of the remaining group stage fixtures but failed to score as Germany were eliminated at the first round for the first time since 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timo_Werner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nicknamed "Turbo Timo", Werner is known for his acceleration and pace.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> A direct, hard-working, and energetic <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forward</a>, he initially played as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a> in his youth, before being switched to a striker or <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Centre-forward" title="Forward (association football)">centre-forward</a> role. An intelligent player, he has been praised in the media for his determination and willingness to drop deep to retrieve the ball or link-up with midfielders. While he is not known for his physicality, aerial game, or holdup play, he is a prolific goalscorer, possessing excellent movement off the ball, as well as a powerful and accurate shot with his right foot from both inside and outside the penalty area; he usually prefers to cut inside from the left flank and shoot on goal with his stronger foot, although he is also capable of cutting inside from the right and striking with his left.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timo_Werner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
